[16/12/24, 4:58:30 PM] ~â€¯NikeshğŸ–¤âœ¨: On the martyrdom of Somnath Suryawanshi

After the replica of the constitution was vandalised in Parbhani, the Ambedkarites in Parbhani resorted to public demonstrations. The public demonstrations show that the protesters regarded constitution as the most sacred book and it is rightly so. For the constitutionalism built India into a democratic republic. Underlying constitutionalism are the principles of democracy, federalism, and separation of powers. It also includes the rights of the citizens vis a vis the state. The right to criticise the government and uphold the constitution is not just the duty of the Ambedkarite but every citizen of India. It is pathetic that only Ambedkarite rose to protest in the defence of the constitution. Whenever the mob protests, in all likelihood, it creates the turmoil and at times leads to destruction of the private property. However this can not be considered as violence. The protestors did not turn violent though they were defending the very existence of India by registering their unacceptance of anti-India forces bent on destroying India by the destroying the constitution that constituted India. 

The administration and that too police administration must have the highest refrain and must act in a non violent ways to stop the mob from turning violent. The brutal force that police administration used in Parbhani against the honest defenders of the constitution is unacceptable. The protesters could be easily dealt with by the rule of law not by the arbitrary use of the brutal violent force. The images of police beating men and women in Parbhani are shocking and they can be seen in the regimes that are based on violence and violent ideologies. 

Somnath Suryawanshi was an upcoming lawyer and he understood what was at stake when the constitution was vandalised. As a law student, he was well aware of the right to protest and right to criticize the government as the fundamental right of every citizen. The post-mortem examination shows that he succumbed to the multiple injuries caused by the brutal violent by the police. As we can create the situation in the custody, brother Somnath must be asserting his rights in the face of the brutality of the police and often untrained police made a mockery of the upcoming lawyer by using brutal force that killed him eventually. Now imagine hundreds who are held in the police custody and what would be happening to them. 

People at large are questioning the validity of the recently held elections in Maharashtra and there is an eerie silence after the election results. People at large are loosing faith in the government institutions and that too in the election commission of India which is an office created under the constitution and supposed to act in the interest of the nation and not in the interest of the political parties. The ECI should have taken note of peopleâ€™s rising concerns over the election results. 

Why is it to be addressed? 

The citizens should have unshakeable faith in the institutions of government. Martyr Somnath Suryawanshi expressed his discontent, in his discontent lies his love for his country and the constitution that created it. His discontent expressed his deep love for India and the state failed him by killing him brutally at the very site that should protect its citizens. As reported by the police to the journalists that Somnath was not Buddhist but came from Vadar community. Youths in the Vadar community are getting awakened and the movement is not just confined to the Buddhists in Maharashtra and it never was. When Babasaheb Ambedkar was leading the movement for democracy, all the suffering castes joined. The greatest stumbling block in the realisation of the social democracy in India is the â€œdouble consciousnessâ€ of the OBCs, the Shudras who are the foot soldiers of the Brahmins and every now and then are slammed by the Brahmins and kept away from power but they are in the forefront to slam the Scheduled castes though they should be working with them to destroy the hegemony of the Brahmins. In reality, the entire India should rise and acknowledge the martyrdom of Somnath as the defender of Indian constitution and of the Indian nation itself. 

Long live the courage of brother Somnath to offer his life for the country that itself killed him!

Dr. Babasaheb Ambedkar's Jayanti stands apart. It is a celebration that unites across caste, religion, gender, and geography. No other figure in Indian history has impacted as many lives across such a vast spectrum. From drafting the Constitution to empowering women, from water resource policies to the establishment of institutions like RBI, from championing labor rights to fighting untouchability - Dr. Ambedkar's contributions touch every Indian, directly or indirectly.

Yet, Babasaheb's legacy continues to be challenged - not by facts, but by propaganda. Casteism, fake historical narratives, and cultural superiority complexes continue to dominate public discourse. Every caste atrocity, every denial of dignity, every incident of systemic exclusion is a reminder that the fight he began is far from over.

This April 14th, as we celebrate the birth of the architect of modern India, let's not just wear blue - let's wear courage, awareness, and unity.
